# next_steps.md — Living session context

**Purpose.** Cross-session memory for Claude Code: where the last session left off, what's in flight, the umbrella goal, and the immediate next actions. Code-derivable facts live in CLAUDE.md; *state-derivable* facts (uncommitted work, decisions deferred to "next time", critical-path ordering) live here.

**Companion docs:** [`docs/user-stories.md`](./user-stories.md) (what + why) · [`docs/implementation.md`](./implementation.md) (how + in what order, with milestone status + concrete schema / API / file shapes). This file points at the next concrete thing to do; the others are the canonical references.

**Session protocol** (referenced from CLAUDE.md):
- **At session start** — read this file in full before doing anything else. If "In-progress work" conflicts with what's on disk now (file deleted, commit landed, etc.), update this file before continuing.
- **At session end** — update the sections below: move finished items into "Recently completed" (keep last 3–5), refresh "Critical path" and "Immediate next actions", note anything the user deferred.
- **Date format** — absolute ISO dates (`2026-05-14`), never relative phrasings.

---

- **Date:** 2026-06-09 (**Two more OQ conventions added to the TEMPLATE ONLY (per user "update the templates first and I'll let you know when to edit closed-jobs"); `closed-jobs-feature.html` deliberately NOT touched this turn.**) User: (1) "the options for the OQs are very short and indescriptive — they should each describe the changes they hope to do and its effects, trade-offs, pros and cons — the info I need to decide"; (2) "OQ7 has sub-decisions but they look like the exclusively-selectable options of the other OQs … make them each their own OQs and make that the rule — OQs and their options should only have one option to select from." **TWO NEW RULES (embodied in `_template.design-doc.html` + mirrored to memory `feedback-design-doc-open-questions` + `CLAUDE.md`):** (1) **Descriptive options** — each `<li>` must be self-contained enough to decide on: name the approach, the concrete change it makes + its effect, then `Pros:`/`Cons:`; a bare label ("add a column") is banned. (2) **One OQ = one decision** — options are mutually exclusive, pick exactly one; a fork bundling independent sub-decisions must be split into separate OQs, never listed as one OQ's "options." **CHANGES:** `_template.design-doc.html` (prose rewritten for both rules + all 3 example OQs now show descriptive option bodies with Pros/Cons); `docs/assets/style.css` (`.oq-options li` margin `0.25rem`→`0.5rem` for the longer options). **TODO when user gives go-ahead on closed-jobs:** rewrite all OQ option bodies to be descriptive (change+effect+pros/cons), and **split OQ7 into three OQs** — OQ7 eligibility (`INTERESTED`-only vs +`APPLIED`), a new OQ8 trigger (probe-only vs manual-close-also-cascades), a new OQ9 notification (fold into summary vs per-card row) — renumber accordingly. - **Date:** 2026-06-04 (**Astranis intern application-confirmation email mis-merged onto the user's Muon Space card instead of moving the Astranis card to Applied — two compounding bugs fixed + both DBs repaired; COMMITTED scoped; deployed to BOTH tiers; NOT pushed**). (B) **ATS blocklist gap** — Astranis sends from `no-reply@us.greenhouse-mail.io`; the sender-domain dedup blocklist (`SENDER_DOMAINS` in `lib/applications/relevance.ts`) had `greenhouse.io` (the job-board WEB host) but NOT `greenhouse-mail.io` (the actual MAIL host Greenhouse sends from), so `extractSenderDomain` returned a shared multi-tenant root as a per-employer identity and the senderDomain fallback matched the most-recent `greenhouse-mail.io` row (Muon Space, also Greenhouse). Hermeus worked because its email's role matched its posting exactly → primary lookup hit on the first try. **FIX (B):** added `greenhouse-mail.io` to `SENDER_DOMAINS` (doubles as a positive relevance signal + dedup blocklist via `sender-domain.ts`); fixed the misleading `sender-domain.ts` docstring that documented the bug as correct; added regression asserts to `sender-domain-smoke.ts` (43/43, pins `*.greenhouse-mail.io`→null). **FIX (A) — user chose "lenient lookup fallback" over season-stripping (no migration, keeps term variants distinct):** NEW pure `lib/applications/match-role-subset.ts:findUniqueRoleSuperset(incomingRole, candidates)` — when the strict (company,role) lookup misses, merge into the ONE existing role at that employer whose normalized token set is a STRICT SUPERSET of the email's tokens; **declines when ambiguous** (a generic "Software Engineering Intern" subset of 4 Hermeus specializations → no guess → falls through). Wired into `ingest.ts` between the company-only and senderDomain fallbacks, and PRESERVES the richer stored role on a lenient match (so the email's term-stripped title doesn't overwrite `… (Summer 2026)`). NOT an ABI problem (better-sqlite3 loads; research-cache + arxiv-bucket in the same dir work). **FIX (all 3 requested, shipped to the tree):** (1+2) `lib/shared-sqlite-cache.ts` — NEW `reconcileSchema(db, table, label)` runs in `buildInternalStore` BEFORE preparing statements: `PRAGMA table_info` → compare on-disk columns to the new `TABLE_COLUMNS` const; on mismatch **DROP + rebuild the table LOUDLY** (`[<label>] SCHEMA DRIFT …`) since the data is throwaway, instead of silently disabling; a DROP/CREATE that itself throws still degrades to uncached (correct for a real env failure). `buildInternalStore` now takes `label`; call site updated. `components/{Section,MobileShell}.tsx` remain dirty (not mine — exclude from any commit). **FOLLOW-UP (same session) — calendar-time clustering diagnosed + post-mortem cost claim corrected:** user noticed the ~500 loop calendar events sit at many DIFFERENT times in clusters despite one true interview time. Traced: the gcal event start = `ApplicationEvent.scheduledAt` verbatim (`lib/calendar/sync.ts:74`), and `scheduledAt` = the LLM's `extractedDates[].startsAt` (`lib/applications/ingest.ts:599`) — **no send-time fallback** (no `startsAt` → no event). `lib/email-parser.ts:parseApplicationEmail` calls `generateObject` with **no `temperature`** → model default (non-deterministic). So ~1,100 independent parses (552 emails × dev+prod, cache off → each tier parses separately) → a DISTRIBUTION of extracted times → clusters (recurring LLM misreads: tz shifts, AM/PM flips, anchor-relative guesses). Calendar event descriptions still carry `notes = dateEntry.rawText` (the wording the LLM claims it read) — usable to characterize clusters. **This invalidated the post-mortem §5 claim that a working cache would have zeroed the $0.66:** the cache key includes the per-email send-time anchor (`sentAt`), which varies across the 552 looped emails → distinct keys → NOT collapsible; the cache would only have ~HALVED it by deduping the simultaneous dev+prod fan-out of each single message. Corrected §5 (new "Why the cache barely helped" subsection + a callout explaining the calendar clustering) and §9 (cache scope = duplicate-input spend, NOT the loop fix). **Characterized + written into post-mortem §6 (NEW section "Anatomy of the calendar clutter — a date feedback loop").** Reconstructed from the pre-cleanup backup `~/backups/mission-control/prod.db.pre-mailloop-cleanup-20260602T042424Z` (calendar start = `ApplicationEvent.scheduledAt` verbatim, so the DB mirrors the calendar). Findings: 552 loop INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED events → **399 distinct parsed times spread Feb 6–Jun 3 2026** (real interview = **2026-06-03 11:00 AM**, the LATEST time; all others drifted earlier; monthly histogram Feb 99/Mar 149/Apr 139/May 143/Jun 22). Mechanism = THREE compounding bugs: (1) the INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED notification body is `event.scheduledAt.toLocaleString()` (`lib/repositories/applicationEvents.ts:61`) → each self-email re-encodes the prior parse's time (550/552 rawTexts are `toLocaleString`-shaped `M/D/YYYY, h:mm:ss AM/PM`; the only 2 exceptions are the genuine human seeds incl. `06/03/2026 at 11:00 AM`); (2) the LLM inconsistently serialized the zone-less wall-clock time as UTC vs local — EVERY drifted rawText resolved to a ±7h (PDT, 106) / ±8h (PST, 36) pair = Pacific's season-correct offset (definitive proof of local↔UTC confusion, not random jitter); (3) 552 iterations random-walked the date backward ~117 days. So the answer to the user's "LLM or something else?" = BOTH: LLM tz-misserialization fueled by an app-side feedback loop. Added prevention item §10 (make date extraction tz-safe + stop embedding a re-parseable timestamp in notification bodies) and flagged bug #2 as LATENT beyond the loop (a single genuine interview can land 7–8h off). Renumbered post-mortem cross-refs (old §6–9 → §7–10) to make room for the inserted §6; structure verified (11 `details.section` balanced; 10 `h2` ids == 10 TOC links; §-refs all in range). Analysis ran against a throwaway copy of the backup in `$CLAUDE_JOB_DIR/tmp` — the backup itself untouched. **FOLLOW-UP (same session) — restarts + live Gmail/Calendar cleanup (user: "first do the restarts required for both services then clean up my gmail and gcal"):** (1) **Restarted all 4 PM2 procs** (`mission-control`, `mission-control-dev`, `mission-control-scheduler-prod/-dev`) — all online; cache now works against the already-repaired `data/llm-cache.db` (schema `key,value,status,expiry,reserved_at,done_at` confirmed live; no `[llm-cache] disabled` lines post-restart). NOTE: the prod APP runs the compiled 06-02 bundle (no `reconcileSchema` until a rebuild) but works because the file is fixed; the 3 source-run procs (dev app via turbopack + both schedulers via tsx) have the auto-heal. (2) **Calendar cleaned:** the loop only synced calendar events for FUTURE `scheduledAt` (`ingest.ts:463` gate), and the drift walked backward into the past, so only **28 events** (14 prod + 14 dev, all dated 6/2–6/3) ever reached gcal — NOT ~500 (the ~500 were emails + DB rows). Calendar event id = `sha1(ApplicationEvent.id)` (`gcalIdempotencyId`, validated against the 14 stored gcalEventIds). Deleted **27** loop events via MCP `delete_event` (the 28th, `cbef3bfe…`, the user had already deleted); 2 were transiently denied by the auto-mode classifier (near the genuine interview) and succeeded on retry. LEFT both (genuine, not loop) — flagged to user to pick which to keep. - **Date:** 2026-06-04 (**NewPostingsCard location filter leaked Canada via the ", CA" state-code needle — boundary-aware recheck; COMMITTED scoped (`da461b1`); NOT pushed; dev-only HMR**). User (on dev): "the location filter in newpostingscard seems to not be working correctly … showing me things from canada which is neither in california or los angeles which are the two location filters i have." (Employment-type filter — `intern` — worked fine.) **Root cause:** the `California` chip expands (in `lib/postings/location-expansion.ts:expandLocationFilter`) to the needles `["California", ", CA"]`; the `/api/postings` route matched each via Prisma `location: { contains: n }` → SQLite `LIKE`, which is **case-insensitive AND unanchored**, so the bare `, CA` needle matched the *prefix* of `, Canada` / `, CAN`. Confirmed against dev.db: of 189 distinct `status='new'` locations the loose prefilter caught for `California`+`Los Angeles`, exactly 5 were Canadian false positives (`Toronto, CAN`, `CAN - Richmond/Petawawa/Winnipeg, Canada`, `Cambridge, Ontario, Canada`). The employment filter was immune because it's an exact enum `in` match, not a substring. **Fix (kept the loose `LIKE` as a cheap *superset* prefilter so the candidate set stays bounded in SQL — that's why filtering was pushed server-side originally — then tighten in JS):** NEW `lib/postings/location-expansion.ts:locationMatchesChips(location, chips)` — re-applies the chips with word-boundary semantics: a bare 2-letter code-suffix needle (`/^, [a-z]{2}$/` → `, CA`/`, NY`/`, ON`/`, UK`…) must be followed by end-of-string or a non-letter (scans **every** occurrence, so a multi-location string like `…Ontario, CAN; San Francisco, CA` still matches on the genuine `, CA`); city needles (`Long Beach`, `Glendale, CA`) and literals (`California`, `United States`) keep plain `includes`. `app/api/postings/route.ts` GET renamed the negative-filter result to `negativeFiltered` and adds, when `locations.length>0`, a `.filter(r => locationMatchesChips(r.location, locations))` pass (applies even under `includeFiltered` — a location chip is an explicit user filter). Because the matcher only TIGHTENS code needles, the SQL `LIKE` stays a strict superset → the post-fetch pass can only drop false positives, never a true match, never under-fetch. **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` exit 0; `location-expansion-smoke` **39/39** (added 4 cases: California ⊅ the 5 Canada strings, ⊇ `Long Beach, CA`/mixed-CAN-with-real-CA, LA-metro, US-country ⊅ `Toronto, CAN`, empty-chips/null-location); real-data run over dev.db dropped exactly the 5 Canadian locations, kept all 184 genuine CA/LA. **COMMITTED** as `da461b1` — ONLY my 3 files (`lib/postings/location-expansion.ts`, `app/api/postings/route.ts`, `scripts/tests/hermetic/location-expansion-smoke.ts`). **NOT pushed** (user didn't ask; push runs the full hermetic gate). Server-side change is LIVE on dev :4101 via Turbopack HMR, but React Query caches per-filter — **refresh / toggle the filter to refetch**. The concurrent watchlist-dedup job committed its work mid-session (its `app/api/watchlists/route.ts` / `NewPostingsCard.tsx` / `duplicate-boards.ts` / `pre-push.sh` churn left the tree between my reads); `components/{Section,MobileShell}.tsx` remain dirty (not mine — exclude from any commit).

- **Date:** 2026-06-02 (**Self-notification mail-loop FIX — root-caused a 551-email spam blast, shipped a 2-signal ingest guard + free-mail dedup block, cleaned both DBs, REBUILT + REDEPLOYED prod; NOT committed; NOT pushed**). **[Correction 2026-06-04: superseded — this fix was subsequently committed as `7ae5a6c` ("break self-notification mail loop + senderDomain tiebreaker role guard") AND is now on `origin/main`. Every "NOT committed / NOT pushed" note in this entry is stale.]** User: "why did i get spammed with emails from mission-control?" **Root cause — a mail feedback loop:** `lib/email/send.ts:notificationToEmail` sends notifications FROM→TO the user's OWN Gmail (`from`/`to` both `user.email`, subject `[mission-control] …`). Those land back in the INBOX the Gmail webhook watches → the webhook re-ingests our own outbound mail → the LLM classifies it as a fresh interview → fires another notification → another email → loop. Critical tier bypasses quiet hours; each iteration is a distinct Gmail msgId so the per-message `@@unique(applicationId,emailMsgId,kind)` dedup can't stop it. **Amplifier:** `gmail.com` was NOT on the dedup blocklist (`SENDER_DOMAINS` is ATS-only), so the self-email's From (`…@gmail.com`) resolved to `senderDomain=gmail.com` and the senderDomain *fallback* funneled every re-ingest onto whatever app carried `gmail.com`. **Proven from prod.db + logs:** 552 INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED events on ONE CalSAWS app, 552 distinct inbound msgIds, **1,102 webhook deliveries in a 20-min window (2026-06-02 03:29–03:49 UTC)**; the EMAIL_RECEIVED event titles were literally `[mission-control] California Statewide…`; log line `[ingest] sender-domain fallback matched … domain=gmail.com → app=…CalSAWS`. **Seed** = a real CalSAWS interview reminder at 03:26:42. **What halted it:** Gmail's own send throttle (`User-rate limit exceeded … (Mail sending)`), NOT our code — so it was dormant-not-fixed (could recur on any new genuine notification). **Confirmed NOT caused by tests** — hermetic smokes run on dev.db with `EMAIL_ENABLED=0` on throwaway users; the loop ran on the deployed prod bundle via the realtime webhook (logs show only `[GMAIL WEBHOOK]`, zero `[BACKFILL]`). **FIX (code):** NEW `lib/applications/self-notification.ts` (`isSelfNotificationEmail` + `MC_NOTIFICATION_HEADER="X-Mission-Control"` / `MC_NOTIFICATION_HEADER_VALUE="notification"` / `MC_SUBJECT_PREFIX="[mission-control] "`); `lib/email/send.ts` now stamps the `X-Mission-Control: notification` header on every notification (EmailMessage gained `headers?`; `buildRfc822Message` emits them) + uses `MC_SUBJECT_PREFIX`; `lib/applications/ingest.ts` skips with `reason:"self_notification"` BEFORE `looksRelevant`/classifier (checks the header primarily, the subject-prefix as fallback for pre-header mail already in the inbox); NEW `FREE_MAIL_DOMAINS` in `lib/applications/relevance.ts` (20 consumer roots) folded into `sender-domain.ts`'s `BLOCKED_ROOTS` — **blocklist-only, deliberately NOT added to `SENDER_DOMAINS`** (that list doubles as a positive relevance signal; widening it would flood the classifier with personal mail). **TESTS:** NEW `self-notification-loop-guard-smoke.ts` (20/20 — matrix, closed-loop round-trip through notificationToEmail→buildRfc822→isSelfNotification, free-mail-blocked-but-not-relevant, source guards) added to `pre-push.sh`; extended `sender-domain-smoke.ts` (free-mail→null, 41/41). **Full hermetic gate 101/101; `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors.** **DATA CLEANUP (user-authorized via question; both DBs backed up `~/backups/mission-control/{prod,dev}.db.pre-mailloop-cleanup-20260602T042424Z`):** loop = self-notif emails leaked onto **4 prod apps** (CalSAWS, Bell Smoke [test], Delta Air Lines, LA Dodgers) / **2 dev apps**; deleted **1,229 prod + 668 dev** loop ApplicationEvents (all kinds sharing a `[mission-control]%`-titled EMAIL_RECEIVED msgId) + **559 prod + 323 dev** loop Notifications + nulled the free-mail `senderDomain` magnets. Genuine events preserved (CalSAWS back to APPLIED×1/EMAIL_RECEIVED×2/INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED×2, status INTERVIEW); 0 orphan notifications on prod (15 pre-existing May-17–20 dev orphans left as out-of-scope). **DEPLOYED:** `npm run build` (clean, `self_notification` confirmed in `.next/server`), `pm2 restart mission-control` + `mission-control-dev` — both tiers HTTP 200, guard LIVE. - **Date:** 2026-06-02 (**arXiv 429 recovery — cross-tier cooldown circuit breaker + graceful empty degradation; COMMITTED to main; NOT pushed**). User: "lots of errors with arXiv" + research routes 500ing in dev. **Root cause:** the shipped 3-layer fix ([`docs/arxiv-rate-limit-fix.html`](./arxiv-rate-limit-fix.html)) only *reduces* arXiv load — none of the 3 layers *recovers* once arXiv has already IP-throttled us (the doc says so: "no layer is load-bearing for correctness"). Proven with a raw `curl` bypassing all our code → `429 "Rate exceeded."` regardless of User-Agent. Mechanism: fresh week (no pick persisted yet → review/historical fall through to a fresh arXiv *search*) → 429 → route 500 → `withSharedCache` correctly refuses to cache the error → next dash load re-fires the search → arXiv's throttle window keeps resetting → **block never clears**. Non-causes ruled out: the shared bucket IS pacing (all 4 procs log `[arxiv-bucket] ready … 14/min`); schedulers don't touch arXiv; better-sqlite3 loads. **Fix (extends Layer 3; every piece best-effort + rollback-safe):** (1) NEW `lib/arxiv/errors.ts` — `ArxivUnavailableError` + `ArxivRateLimitCooldownError extends` it. (2) `lib/arxiv/rate-limit.ts` — a cross-tier cooldown row (`arxiv_cooldown(id=1, until)`) in the SAME shared bucket file + a per-process fallback var; `noteArxivRateLimited(ms?)` MAX-extends it (race-safe in SQL), `acquireArxivSlot()` fast-fails with `ArxivRateLimitCooldownError` (zero arXiv calls) while active. Default `ARXIV_COOLDOWN_MS=900000` (15 min, user-chosen; env-tunable). (3) NEW `lib/arxiv/fetch.ts:fetchArxivXml(url)` — ONE helper that paces, detects a 429 / plaintext "Rate exceeded" 200, trips the cooldown, and returns the Atom XML (throws `ArxivUnavailableError`). Replaced the duplicated acquire→fetch→checks dance in EVERY arXiv caller: review + historical (both the fresh-search and legacy `id_list` paths), the listings route (now `parser.parseString(await fetchArxivXml())` instead of `parseURL` — gains 429 detection), and the user-initiated `import` route. (4) `lib/research/shared-cache.ts` — new `fallbackOnError?(err)` option on `withSharedCache`: on a cold-cache compute failure with NO stale, serve the mapped payload (200, **uncached** so the next request retries) instead of rethrowing → 500; also guarded the follower `await pending` so a leader failure degrades the followers instead of 500ing them. The 4 routes pass `fallbackOnError: err => err instanceof ArxivUnavailableError ? [] : undefined` and re-throw `ArxivUnavailableError` from their `catch` (genuine non-arXiv bugs still 500). **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; `arxiv-shared-bucket-smoke` **12/12** (added cooldown cross-tier-visibility + extend-only + acquire-fast-fail scenarios; existing pacing/refill/fallback preserved), `research-shared-cache-smoke` **14/14**, `api-docs-smoke` in sync (TTLs unchanged). **End-to-end LIVE on dev :4101:** all 3 research routes return HTTP 200 with real data (arXiv recovered the moment we stopped hammering — exactly the behavior the cooldown now enforces), and this-week's picks (`weekStart 1780297200000`) are now persisted WITH metadata → Layer 2 takes over → ~0 steady-state arXiv calls. **COMMITTED to main — ONLY my files** (`lib/arxiv/{errors,fetch,rate-limit}.ts`, `lib/research/shared-cache.ts`, the 4 research routes, the bucket smoke, this doc + the design doc + CLAUDE.md). `.env.{development,production}` got the `ARXIV_COOLDOWN_MS=900000` line on-disk but those files are **gitignored** (`.gitignore: .env*`) so they're NOT in the commit — the code default (`900000`, 15 min) matches, so no functional gap; a `pm2 restart --update-env` would only be needed to override the default. **EXCLUDED the concurrent agent's leftover churn** (`components/Section.tsx`, `components/dashboard/MobileShell.tsx` — still dirty; their `Application.location` work already landed as `2d1f3a3`). **NOT pushed** (push runs the full hermetic gate against the working tree, which still carries the other agent's uncommitted changes). The `Error in applications backfill: … Unique constraint failed on (userId, normalizedCompany, normalizedRole, track)` in dev logs is the other agent's Gmail-ingest path — NOT arXiv.

- **Date:** 2026-06-01 (**Rocket Lab duplicate-card root cause → Fix A (lookup fallback) + Fix B (normalizedCompany NOT NULL) + a hermetic test for each; 3 user-data merges; BOTH DBs migrated; prod rebuilt + redeployed; COMMITTED + PUSHED**). User: why did the RocketLab "Software Intern" career app spawn a NEW kanban card instead of moving the existing one? **Root cause:** the existing card (`cmpi1yvwa`, tracked-from-posting 2026-05-23) had **`normalizedCompany = NULL`** (a track-as-application row created before the inline-normalize fix; a later backfill filled `normalizedRole` but not `normalizedCompany` → the unanticipated *NULL-company + concrete-role* state). That single NULL defeated **all four** dedup layers in `lib/applications/ingest.ts`: (1) `findApplicationByCompanyAndRole` strict-equality on `normalizedCompany="Rocket Lab"` missed the NULL; (2) the `findApplicationByCompany` fallback *found* it via `LOWER(company)` but its accept-gates (`!normalizedRole` OR roleless email) both fail when row+email each carry a concrete role → rejected; (3) senderDomain fallback missed (old row never stamped a domain); (4) the `@@unique(...normalizedCompany...)` backstop is NULL-distinct in SQLite so the create didn't even P2002. User pushed back that a backfill "just changes the db, doesn't fix why it missed" — correct. **Fix A** (`lib/repositories/applications.ts:findApplicationByCompanyAndRole`): added a second-stage `LOWER(company)` + **strict-`normalizedRole`** + track raw fallback (mirrors `findApplicationByCompany`) so a stale/empty/NULL/drifted company key can't silently miss a same-role match, while a genuinely-different role stays a distinct row (multi-role-per-company preserved) and a roleless row (NULL `normalizedRole`) still falls through. Rewrote the function's now-false docstring (it had claimed the fallback was "intentionally not present"). Verified against real dev data: the fallback matches `cmpi1yvwa` at bug-time state. Fix A *also* repairs the same miss in `track-as-application` (same helper). **Fix B** (prevention): backfilled `normalizedCompany` (existing `scripts/backfill-normalized-company.ts` — never run on dev.db till now) + made the column **NOT NULL** (new migration `20260601224445_require_application_normalized_company`, applied via `migrate deploy` after stopping the two dev-tier PM2 procs to clear the SQLite lock; schema.prisma updated, client regenerated, dev procs restarted). Now a create path that bypasses `normalizeCompanyName` fails *loudly at the insert* instead of silently producing a dedup-defeating row. **Two real user-data duplicates merged** (both this bug's fallout, both Rocket Lab career, surfaced as backfill conflicts): "Software Intern Fall 2026" (the reported one — folded the email card `cmpvs000r` APPLIED+senderDomain into the original `cmpi1yvwa`, which is now APPLIED with the email's 3-event timeline) and a second hidden pair "Mission Operation Intern Fall 2026" (`cmpkue42b`→`cmpi1ys7z`). Final: 6 Rocket Lab cards, all `normalizedCompany` set, zero dup triples. **Tests:** NEW `find-app-by-company-role-stale-key-smoke.ts` (8/8 — Fix A: empty/drifted-key match, different-role stays distinct, roleless not caught, indexed path, track+cross-user scoping) and NEW `normalized-company-not-null-smoke.ts` (6/6 — Fix B: client rejects null/omitted, DB raw-INSERT NULL hits the NOT NULL constraint, paired positive controls), both in `pre-push.sh`. **Fallout fixed:** NOT NULL broke raw `application.create` in hermetic tests — updated `contacts`/`stale-nudge`/`deadline-nudge`/`bulk-track` (its §5 "null normalizedCompany" reframed to "null normalizedRole", still-nullable) + `find-app-by-company-smoke` (rows now carry an unmatchable sentinel so it still exercises the `LOWER(company)` fallback); `backfill-normalized-company.ts` candidate query switched to raw SQL (typed findMany can't express `normalizedCompany: null` post-NOT-NULL). **Full hermetic gate 99/99; `tsc --noEmit` clean.** **Prod rebuilt + redeployed:** `npm run build` (clean), prod.db backed up (`~/backups/mission-control/prod.db.pre-normalizedcompany-notnull-20260601T163055`), prod-tier procs stopped → backfilled prod.db (16 NULLs) → merged its one conflict (a third duplicate: **Vast / Security Officer / side**, `cmpj4qmly`→`cmpj4oz8h`, identical `sourceJobId` — same job tracked twice 1 min apart) → `migrate deploy` → restarted `mission-control` + `mission-control-scheduler-prod`. - **Date:** 2026-06-01 (**Resume "Re-render" false 429 — RAH-12 rate limiter scoped to actual cost; COMMITTED scoped; NOT pushed; prod NOT rebuilt**). User: clicking the canon **"Re-render"** button (a deterministic, non-LLM render) errored "you've been doing this too much". **Root cause:** `app/api/resumes/route.ts` POST ran the RAH-12 Gemini-budget limiter (`checkUserRateLimit("resumes:gen", …)`, **5 gens / 10 min**) at the very TOP of the handler — before the body was even parsed — so it fired for **every** request regardless of type. The re-render path (canon render with `options.rewrite`/`options.tagline` OFF = the default) is provably **zero-Gemini** (verified: `generateCanonManualResume` skips `rewriteBullets`/`tailorResumeTagline`, `resolveSelection` runs unscored, render/`computeSkillsGap` touch no `acquireGeminiSlot`/`chatJSON`), so iterating in the builder burned the 5/10min cap and surfaced a paid-budget 429 for an op that spends none. **Fix:** parse the body FIRST (pure, no side effects), then scope the limiter to real cost — **Gemini-touching** requests (url/text/application auto-pipeline, OR a canon render with rewrite/tagline opted in) keep the tight `resumes:gen` 5/10min cap; **verbatim canon re-render** (canonId set + both AI toggles off) gets a separate generous `resumes:render` **60/10min** cap that still bounds a true runaway/refresh loop (PDF render is CPU-heavy under the 2 GB worker cap — preserves the original defense-in-depth intent) without blocking manual iteration. Error noun now reads "re-renders" vs "generations" to match the path. **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0); `user-rate-limit-smoke` **14/14** (the smoke tests the pure fn, not the route wiring, so the reorder is safe). **COMMITTED scoped** to `app/api/resumes/route.ts` + this doc; **EXCLUDED** the concurrent job's `docs/architecture.html` (M). **NOT pushed** (a push currently fails the api-docs gate until the concurrent project-dates work regenerates `apis.html`; my change does NOT alter the API surface so `apis.html` is unaffected by it). Live on dev :4101 via Turbopack HMR; **prod :3101 NOT rebuilt** — needs `npm run build` + `pm2 restart mission-control`.

- **Date:** 2026-06-01 (**Watchlist/canon keywords → plain comma lists; OR/quotes added only at fetch time; migration applied to BOTH DBs + both schedulers redeployed; COMMITTED scoped; NOT pushed**). User wanted to stop typing/seeing boolean `"phrase" OR "phrase"` syntax in watchlists + canon — the app should add OR/quotes itself ("for me it's implied it's OR; we're trying to catch as much as possible"). **Root cause confirmed:** the LinkedIn/Indeed fetchers send `config.keywords` **verbatim** to the guest search APIs (`keywords=` / `q=`), which treat a bare comma list as implicit-AND (NARROWS), not OR (BROADENS) — commas alone would silently tank results; the conversion must live in our code. **Shipped (single chokepoint):** NEW `lib/watchlists/keyword-query.ts:buildSearchQuery(raw)` — reuses `splitCanonKeywords` (splits on OR/comma/semicolon/newline, strips quotes/parens, dedupes) then quotes multi-word terms + joins with ` OR ` (single-word terms left bare). **Idempotent on legacy boolean strings**, so un-migrated rows keep working. Wired into BOTH `lib/fetchers/{linkedin,indeed}-fetcher.ts` — the ONLY callers are `scheduler/jobs/job-watcher.ts`; the **web tier never runs them, so NO `npm run build`/web restart needed.** **Storage + UI stay list-form:** canon tokenizer (`lib/canons/keywords.ts`) comment updated; canon keyword placeholders OR→comma (`CanonsCard.tsx` ×2 — **this 2-line edit got swept into the concurrent commit `a93a4f1`, confirmed present in HEAD**); `EditFindRolesModal` keyword input gained a comma placeholder; `AddWatchlistModal` advanced keyword placeholder → comma form (the find-roles placeholders were ALREADY comma form — backend wasn't honoring them, a latent bug this fixes). **Migration:** NEW `scripts/migrate-keywords-to-comma.ts` (dry-run default, `--write`; rewrites `Watchlist.config.keywords` linkedin/indeed + `Canon.keywords` boolean→comma via splitCanonKeywords + join `, `) — applied `--write` to **BOTH dev.db + prod.db: 4 watchlists + 4 canons each**; idempotent re-run = 0. **Both schedulers redeployed** (`pm2 restart mission-control-scheduler-{dev,prod}` — tsx-on-source, restart IS the deploy) so the new conversion runs **before the next crawl tick** (else the just-migrated comma form would've been sent raw to LinkedIn/Indeed = the broken case); prod scheduler booted clean (11 jobs, ready). **Verified:** NEW hermetic `keyword-query-smoke.ts` 7/7 wired into `pre-push.sh` SUITES; `canon-keyword-split-smoke` still 7/7; `tsc --noEmit` clean on touched files; Root cause: the em dash (U+2014) in the canon name flowed into `Content-Disposition: filename="…"` (a ByteString — codepoints >255 throw), so building the response threw and the canon handler returned it as the 500. `lib/resumes/labels.ts:sanitizeFilenameSegment` now folds typographic punctuation to ASCII (em/en dashes→`-`, smart quotes→`'`, ellipsis→`...`) and drops any remaining codepoint >255, **keeping Latin-1 accents** (José/Café ≤255 survive). Migration `20260601120000_add_project_dates` (hand-authored additive `ALTER TABLE "Project" ADD COLUMN` ×2; used `migrate deploy` not `migrate dev` — deterministic, no shadow-DB reset risk on the mailbox-equiv prod.db) applied to **BOTH dev.db + prod.db** (prod.db backed up first → `~/backups/mission-control/prod.db.pre-project-dates-20260601T003035`; each tier's web+scheduler momentarily stopped to dodge the PM2 SQLite lock, migrated, `prisma generate`, restarted; dev :4101 + prod :3101 both back to 200). **Zod** (`lib/schemas/profile.ts`): added `startDate`/`endDate` to `ProjectSchema` (**`.nullable().optional()`** — same `scratchpad` precedent so pre-migration snapshots/fixtures validate without churn) + `ProjectPostSchema` + `ProjectPatchSchema`. **Repo** (`lib/repositories/profile.ts`): `ProjectCreateInput`/`ProjectUpdateInput` + create/update payloads (copied Education's). **Route** (`app/api/profile/projects/route.ts`): POST/PATCH ISO-string→`Date` conversion (PATCH preserves the `undefined`-passthrough). **UI** (`components/ui/ProjectRow.tsx`): Start/End `<input type=date>` rows w/ `dateToInput`/`inputToIso` helpers + `placeholder="Present"` (mirrors `EducationRow`). **Render** (`lib/resumes/templates/ats-plain.tsx`): per user's pick (AskUserQuestion — option C), **date + links share the right column on one line** → `"<start> – <end|Present> · Repo · Website"`; date renders **only when `startDate` present** (dateless legacy projects emit links-only, NO `"? – Present"` placeholder). - **Date:** 2026-05-31 (**Resume-generator redesign — DESIGN DOC `docs/resume-manual-builder.html` written + 4 core forks decided with the user; COMMITTED scoped; NO code yet, NOT pushed**). User: "the resume generator isn't really that good — no reason my security-guard experience should be on an ML/AI Engineering resume." Root cause confirmed in code: `lib/resumes/select.ts:scoreBullet` selects bullets by **keyword-overlap count** (`TAG_WEIGHT=2`/`SUBSTRING_WEIGHT=1`) — a fundamental ceiling that can't tell domain-relevant from irrelevant (a guard bullet matches soft ML words like *communication/data/reporting*), and the **work-role spine** (`pickWorkRoleSpineIndex`+`dropZeroScoreEntities`) + **all-education-kept** rules force the latest job in at zero score. **Direction (user's): a MANUAL per-Canon selector** — show the whole profile, hand-pick bullets, lock entities. **Key architectural fit:** the Canon already owns a reusable resume whose fixed selection lives in `GeneratedResume.selections` (flat JSON), and `lib/canons/specialize.ts:reconstructSelection` already rebuilds a nested `ResumeSelection` from stored rows + a frozen profile snapshot (dropping deleted entities). So the redesign = **replace the Canon's "Regenerate" auto-pipeline with a hand-edited selection**; reuse render/specialize/persist/staleness/versioning verbatim. **4 forks DECIDED (AskUserQuestion):** (OQ1) manual selection core, **AI rewrite + tagline opt-in toggles, default off** (verbatim render); (OQ2) **per-entity lock** (🔒 always / out), NOT per-section-type; (OQ3) selection **saved per-Canon**, re-renderable ("ML resume" vs "Security resume" = separate selections); (OQ4) old scoring pipeline survives as a **"Suggest from posting"** pre-fill button (a guess you edit, not the decider). **Proposed data model:** new nullable `Canon.selection` JSON column — `{version, sectionOrder, sectionsOff[], entities:{<id>:{kind,state,bulletIds[]}}, extras}` with per-entity `state ∈ {always, auto, never}` (the `never` state is the structural fix — `selectBullets`/spine/Suggest can't re-add a guard job set to `never`). **9 OPEN OQs (OQ5–OQ13) in the doc, leans recorded, NOT yet resolved with user — NO code until they are; OQ5/OQ6/OQ7 gate Phase 1 (data model):** OQ5 entity-state cardinality (lean 3-state always/auto/never), OQ6 storage (lean single JSON column), OQ7 bullet granularity (lean per-bullet checkboxes), OQ8 ordering (lean inherit profile order, defer drag), OQ9 length (lean drop one-page auto-prune in manual mode + post-render page count), OQ10 UI surface (lean Window-class overlay from the Canon row), OQ11 Suggest input (lean both canon-keywords + pasted posting), OQ12 fate of the one-off `GenerateResumeCard` (lean keep for now), OQ13 rewrite scope when on (lean keep today's no-match passthrough). **Doc follows the `_template.design-doc.html` archetype** (context → design+Mermaid+touch-list+alternatives → risks&rollback → Open Questions → 4-phase Tasks P1–P4 with ≥2 nesting levels); validated (ToC↔ids 1:1, `<details>` 26/26 balanced, no inline `<style>`, no literal `\n` in Mermaid, 4 decided `callout tip` + 9 open `callout`). **Touch list (for when code starts):** `prisma/schema.prisma` (+`Canon.selection`, migrate dev.db+prod.db), `lib/schemas/canons.ts`, `lib/repositories/canons.ts`, NEW `lib/canons/selection.ts` (`resolveSelection`+`suggestPrefill`), NEW `app/api/canons/[id]/selection/route.ts`, branch in `app/api/resumes/route.ts`, NEW `components/overlays/ResumeBuilderOverlay.tsx`, `CanonsCard.tsx`, regen `apis.html`, hermetic smoke. **COMMITTED scoped to `docs/resume-manual-builder.html` + this entry ONLY** — concurrent other-job `docs/architecture.html` (M) EXCLUDED. **NOT pushed. NEXT: resolve OQ5–OQ13 with the user (start with the data-model trio OQ5/6/7), then begin Phase 1.**

- **Date:** 2026-05-31 (**AMD news fetcher 404 fix + ALL job fetchers routed through `loggedFetch` for health visibility — 2 commits (`806364e`, `dee32a2`); dev scheduler restarted live; prod scheduler restart DONE; NOT pushed**). Verified the real adapter fetch returns 10 articles. **(2) "why only Greenhouse" — diagnosed, NOT a bug:** `scheduler/jobs/job-watcher.ts:runDueWatchlists` runs every 10-min tick but only fires watchlists whose `lastRunAt` is older than per-watchlist `scheduleMinutes` (dev: almost all **240min/4h**; Anthropic+Rocket Lab greenhouse **60min/1h**; linkedin ~233–251min). At the moment the user looked, **0 were due**; every ATS had run in the prior 1–3.5h. Greenhouse over-represented because it has **23 watchlists** vs ashby/lever/workday 4 + clearcompany 1, plus 2 hourly boards. **(3) Root observability gap (the real find):** ALL 12 job fetchers used **raw `fetch()`** for the discovery (board-listing) call → no `[EXTERNAL API]` line, no fetcher-health row; only the liveness probes (which use `loggedFetch`) were visible, so the Fetcher Health card/log viewer reflected probing volume, not fetch health — and hid breakages (the AMD-class 200-with-changed-shape would read `ok`). **Fix (`dee32a2`, 12 files):** `greenhouse, lever, ashby, workday, smartrecruiters, workable, recruitee, personio, clearcompany, linkedin, indeed, careers-page` all swap `fetch()`→`loggedFetch(url, init, {record:false})` + record exactly ONE outcome per HTTP call (mirrors rss/scrape-fetcher): **error** (HTTP non-2xx / throw / timeout / 429 / 403), **broken** (200 but unparseable — Zod-shape fail, missing XML root, Cloudflare wall), **ok** (fetched+parsed; empty result stays `ok` for the scrapers/careers-page since an empty search is legit). Paginated fetchers (smartrecruiters/clearcompany/workday) record **per page**; partial-crawl semantics preserved. **Observability-only — no fetch contract changed.** **Verified:** `tsc` clean; hermetic `fetcher-unit 72/72`, `fetcher-partial 6/6`, `fetcher-health-store 26/26` (isolated `FETCHER_HEALTH_PATH`); live direct-call test (greenhouse/lever emitted `[EXTERNAL API]` + wrote `ok`/`error` rows); **live on BOTH schedulers** (`pm2 restart mission-control-scheduler-dev` then `-prod --update-env` — schedulers run `scheduler/index.ts` via `tsx` source, so a restart is the whole deploy; dev post-restart tick already logs the LinkedIn **discovery** search URL, previously invisible). Prod web card already reads the store so **NO prod web rebuild needed**. **NOT pushed** (a push runs the full pre-push hermetic gate). **Unrelated pre-existing issue spotted at dev-scheduler boot:** `[llm-cache] disabled — table init failed; running UNCACHED: no such column: value` — the cross-tier LLM dedup cache (`data/llm-cache.db`) is on a stale schema (best-effort so nothing breaks, but cross-tier LLM dedup is OFF until the file's schema is refreshed); flagged to user, NOT addressed.

- **Date:** 2026-05-31 (**Internal Systems · System Telemetry overflow fix + app-wide Section gutter bump — COMMITTED scoped to my 2 files + this doc, tsc clean; NOT pushed**). User reported the **System Telemetry** card (`components/views/InternalView.tsx`) overflowing off the right edge with the last indicators unreachable at md/sm widths. Root cause: the 6 stat tiles were `shrink-0 whitespace-nowrap` with heavy `px-8` inside a `md:flex-nowrap justify-between` row — un-shrinkable AND un-scrollable → clipped. **Fix (iterated live with the user):** tile row → `flex justify-between gap-0 md:gap-8 flex-1 w-full overflow-x-auto custom-scrollbar` (horizontal-scroll safety net so nothing ever clips; **zero gap at sm**, generous auto-distributed gap at md+ via `justify-between`); tiles → `flex flex-col items-center text-center … py-4 px-8 … w-fit shrink-0 whitespace-nowrap` (content-hugging `w-fit` so content isn't dwarfed + centered + `px-8` horizontal breathing room). `custom-scrollbar` already styles horizontal (`height:6px` in `globals.css`). **Spacing convention pinned down with the user (saved as memory `feedback-rem-spacing-convention`):** repo uses **rem via Tailwind's scale** (verified ZERO raw-px padding/margin/gap in `components/`; `px-N` is padding-x in rem, NOT pixels — only `[Npx]` brackets are literal px, reserved for font sizes / fixed dims / shadows) AND **prefer power-of-2 steps** (2/4/8/16; avoid 3/5/6/7). **`components/Section.tsx`** app-wide gutter `mb-8 last:mb-0 px-6` → `last:mb-0 px-8` (user removed `mb-8` themselves mid-session → `last:mb-0` is now vestigial, flagged to them; final gutter is a flat `px-8`). **COMMITTED scoped to `InternalView.tsx` + `Section.tsx` + this doc ONLY** — the concurrent fetcher-health bg job's dirty tree (finance routes, `lib/fetcher-health/`, fetchers, `scheduler/index.ts`, `apis.html`, `pre-push.sh`, untracked `fetcher-health-*` + `arxiv-rate-limit-fix.html`) was EXCLUDED. `tsc --noEmit` clean. - **Date:** 2026-05-31 (**Fetcher Health card — root-caused + full design doc written & reviewed (all 16 OQs decided); scheduler-structured-logs spun out; both design docs COMMITTED; implementation of the fetcher-health store STARTING NEXT**). User flagged the `FetcherHealthCard` showing "No fetcher activity in the last hour / 6h" while the **1d badge read 100%**. **Diagnosed (reproduced the route logic against every PM2 log file):** `app/api/system/fetcher-health/route.ts` lazily **regex-parses ONE PM2 log file** (the *web* process's, picked by `NODE_ENV`) — so it (1) **never sees the scheduler's crawls** (prod scheduler log alone had 2913 `[EXTERNAL API]`/`[CACHE]` markers, all unparseable since the scheduler never runs `initLogger()` → plain text, no `{ts,msg}` JSON), and (2) builds the **per-host table from the last 1h only** while the badges span 1h/6h/1d, so the table empties (firing the "no activity" copy) while a 1d badge still reads 100% off older entries. Plus the route only reads the *current* `out.log` (midnight logrotate truncates the 1d window) and counts "ok" on the *attempt* (logs before the fetch), so a host 500ing on everything reads 100%. **Decision:** replace log-parsing with a dedicated **per-tier, best-effort SQLite store** `data/fetcher-health.db` (gitignored) written at the fetch chokepoints — reusing the cross-*process* better-sqlite3 pattern from `data/llm-cache.db` but per-*tier* by data. NOT a Prisma table in dev/prod.db (the `$allOperations` middleware would log every insert → log-viewer spam; prod.db is mailbox-equivalent + backed up, no place for ephemeral 48h telemetry). **OQ decisions (all 16):** 4 buckets `ok/error/fallback/broken` (a 500 = `error`, recorded from the real `loggedFetch` response; cache hits NOT counted — `cacheStats` already owns hit/miss; no 5th `cache` bucket); per-tier; **web vs scheduler `source` distinction surfaced as an All·Web·Scheduler card filter**; raw events; 48h retention; direct sync write; hostname grouping; near-live TTL + clickable window badges + Error column; start fresh (no backfill); fully delete the log-parsing path; drop the dead `fetcher-health-roll` placeholder; just-color (no notifications — a broader notification system is coming, the `error` bucket is its substrate). **Finance gap found:** `app/api/finance/{route,history/route}.ts` hit Pulsar with bare `fetch()` + relied on `withCache` `upstreamHost` for host attribution — must convert to `loggedFetch` (task P2.1) or Pulsar vanishes from the card. **Docs:** `docs/fetcher-health-store.html` (full plan, §10 P1–P6 checklist) + `docs/scheduler-structured-logs.html` (OQ14 spun out — give the scheduler `initLogger()` for structured stdout + options to surface scheduler logs in the in-app viewer; **6 OQs still OPEN there**). New convention applied: design-doc open questions use **OQ-numbering** (OQ1, OQ2…), not Q. **Committed scoped to ONLY the 2 design docs + this entry** — `components/views/InternalView.tsx` (M) and `docs/arxiv-rate-limit-fix.html` (??) are concurrent other-job work, EXCLUDED. **NEXT: implement `docs/fetcher-health-store.html` §10** — P1 store module first.

- **Date:** 2026-05-29 (employment-type classifier sweep was **~100% broken** — diagnosed + fixed + deployed + **COMMITTED this session** [the commit directly after the dedup `36a0d4d`/`f15f7bf` pair]). Found while reading scheduler logs to verify the dedup work below. **Diagnosed (both tiers):** scheduler-dev had **18 successful per-batch lines but 0 `[employment-type-classifier] DONE`** in an 8000-line window; scheduler-prod 4 failures / 0 DONE. Root cause = two compounding pre-existing bugs (NOT caused by the cache work — the cache logs just surfaced it): (1) the cheapest model (`MODEL_LITE_CHEAP`) intermittently returns a bare array instead of `{types:[...]}` or an out-of-enum value, and the strict `ResultSchema` rejected the **entire 50-item batch**; (2) `classifyEmploymentTypes`'s loop had no per-batch guard, so one bad batch threw the whole sweep AND **discarded every already-classified batch** → `runClassifyPendingEmploymentTypes` persisted **0 rows** despite ~18 good batches, burning ~20 Gemini calls/sweep for nothing. **Fixed (`lib/ai/classify-employment-type.ts`):**
    - **Tolerant `ResultSchema`** (now exported): `z.preprocess` rewraps a bare array → `{types:[...]}`; each element is `z.enum(...).nullable().catch(null)` so an out-of-enum / wrong-case value coerces to null instead of failing the batch. Mirrors the existing count-drift tolerance.
    - **Per-batch isolation** in `classifyEmploymentTypes`: each `classifyOneBatch` is try/caught; a still-failing batch defaults ITS items to null (Unspecified → retried next sweep) and the loop continues. JSDoc + the "throws if any batch fails" contract updated accordingly (job-watcher's inline caller also benefits — it now keeps the good batches instead of falling back to all-Unspecified).
    - **Cache interaction:** a tolerant parse SUCCEEDS so its result is cached (lib/ai/llm-cache.ts) normally; only a genuinely unparseable response (`types` not an array) throws, and that throw is isolated per-batch (not cached → retried). Schema change → cache key changes → today's classifier entries auto-invalidate.
    - `scripts/tests/hermetic/classify-employment-type-smoke.ts` — repurposed the two cases that asserted the OLD throw-on-failure contract: **#5** now tests the tolerant schema directly (bare-array rewrap; `'manager'`/`'Internship'` → null; non-array `types` rejected), **#8** tests per-batch isolation (batch 2 throws → its 50 items null, batches 1+3's 70 survive, no whole-sweep throw). **13/13.**
    - `docs/llm-prompts/employment-type-classifier.md` Notes updated (doc-only — System/User template unchanged, so **no Lunary sync needed**).
    - **Verified:** classify-employment-type-smoke **13/13**, classify-pending-sweep-smoke **9/9**, `tsc` clean. **LIVE (both schedulers restarted):** the dev sweep now **completes + persists** — `DONE 1000 items / 20 batch(es) — 946 classified, 54 null` → `swept 1000 distinct externalIds — 946 classified, 946 rows updated` (was 0/0 before). prod gets the fix on its next sweep (same code; restarted).
- **Date:** 2026-05-29 (cross-tier LLM-call dedup — **implemented + verified + prod redeployed + COMMITTED `36a0d4d`** atop the Gmail Phase 1 commit `1f73067`; the handoff implementation of `docs/cross-tier-llm-dedup.html`, which the Gmail session below wrote for "another agent"). dev (:4101/dev.db) + prod (:3101/prod.db) + both schedulers run the same code on one box against the same data, so every cacheable LLM step called Gemini **twice** for identical input. Three decisions taken via AskUserQuestion up front: (1) **promote `better-sqlite3` to a direct dep** — it was only a transitive *devDependency* via promptfoo and ships no types, so the doc's "zero new deps" wouldn't survive a prod-only install (added `@types/better-sqlite3` devDep too); (2) **caching default-ON with opt-outs**; (3) **full deploy incl. prod redeploy**. **Shipped:**
    - **`lib/ai/llm-cache.ts`** (new) — content-addressed `cacheKey()` (`sha256` of resolved model + system + rendered user prompt + temp + maxOut + `z.toJSONSchema(schema,{io:'input'})`); a **shared WAL SQLite** at `data/llm-cache.db` both tiers open (`busy_timeout=5000`, `synchronous=NORMAL`). `llmCached(req, compute)` runs the reservation protocol: `INSERT OR IGNORE` reserve → **leader** computes; losers **follow** (poll 150ms), **steal** a stale lease (>30s → conditional-UPDATE takeover), or **fall back** to self-compute past 8s. **Best-effort, never load-bearing:** the native binding loads via a guarded dynamic `import()` so an ABI mismatch / unwritable file degrades to direct *uncached* compute (warn once); `compute()` errors propagate untouched and are **never cached** (leader `DELETE`s its reservation + rethrows). `pruneLlmCache()` (60d `done` / 24h crashed-`pending`) + test seams (`_resetLlmCacheForTests`, `_statsForTests`, `_seedPendingForTests`).
    - **`lib/ai/gemini.ts`** — `chatJSON` gains `cache?: boolean` (default `true`); body refactored into a `compute()` closure with **`acquireGeminiSlot()` moved INSIDE it** (only the leader spends a rate token); wraps in `llmCached` unless `cache:false`. **6 generative opt-outs** (`cache:false`): `discovery-suggest`, `bullet-assist-fill`, `bullet-assist-rewrite`, `tagline-draft`, `bullet-tags-from-profile`, `scratchpad-synth` (they re-roll on identical input per the anti-repetition rule). Cached (default): `email-parser`, `employment-type-classifier`, `posting-parse`, `resume-rewrite`, `profile-import`, `profile-synthesize`, `bullet-tags-from-posting`, `resume-tagline`.
    - **`lib/email-parser.ts`** — `loadPrompt` moved before the key (the rendered prompt IS the key); `acquireGeminiSlot` + `generateObject` + `safeTrack` all inside `compute()`, so a cache hit/follower spends no token and is **not** traced as a model call. Keyed on `(MODEL_ID, rendered prompt incl. the sentAt anchor, applicationSchema)` — stable across both webhooks for the same Gmail message (the push fan-out simultaneity case).
    - **`scheduler/jobs/llm-cache-prune.ts`** (new) + registered daily in `scheduler/index.ts` JOBS — **coexists with the Gmail work's `gmail-watch-renew`** entry (the shared-file merge the design doc predicted; both present, no conflict).
    - **`next.config.ts`** — `better-sqlite3` → `serverExternalPackages` (native module, webpack can't bundle). **`.gitignore`** — explicit `data/llm-cache.db*` (also caught by the global `*.db*` globs). **`package.json`** — `better-sqlite3@12.10.0` dep + `@types/better-sqlite3` devDep, installed with `--legacy-peer-deps` (repo has a pre-existing promptfoo↔lunary `openai` peer conflict; no `.npmrc`) + `npm rebuild better-sqlite3` to match the active Node **v24.15.0** ABI (prebuilt binary was ABI 147; all 4 PM2 tiers run v24.15.0, so the rebuild is correct everywhere).

    - **Two design docs written (both new HTML, per the migration convention):**
        - **`docs/gmail-realtime-push.html`** — the wiring plan. Key constraint surfaced mid-design: **dev.db AND prod.db are linked to the same mailbox** (`salsalcedo4321@gmail.com`, refresh token in both), and Gmail permits **one watch per mailbox** — so dev/prod can't point at separate topics (renewals would clobber). Resolution = **one shared topic, two push subscriptions** (fan-out to each tier's webhook).         - **`docs/cross-tier-llm-dedup.html`** — a SEPARATE concern the user wants handed to another agent. Both tiers double-call Gemini for identical input (and run independent per-process rate buckets). Design: content-addressed LLM cache (`sha256(model+rendered prompt+schema)`) in a **shared `better-sqlite3` file** (already installed, zero new deps) with an **in-flight reservation** (leader/follower/steal/fallback) — read-through alone double-misses because the push fan-out fires both tiers simultaneously. - **Date:** 2026-05-29 (SPA / embedded-JSON posting-text fallback — **implemented + verified, COMMITTED `815da88`**). User pasted a Dayforce HCM job URL (`jobs.dayforcehcm.com/en-US/cosm/venues/jobs/5344`) into the resume URL tab and got "the page didn't contain enough to produce a resume." **Diagnosed:** the error is `lib/resumes/posting.ts:parsePosting`'s `rawText.length < MIN_POSTING_TEXT_CHARS` guard. Dayforce is a client-rendered Next.js SPA — 312 KB of HTML, but `fetchVisibleText`'s static fetch + cheerio DOM read returns **0** visible chars (all content is JS-hydrated). The posting IS in the HTML, embedded in the `__NEXT_DATA__` `<script>` blob (which our DOM pass strips). **Fixed:**
    - **`lib/resumes/posting.ts`** — new exported pure fn `extractPostingTextFromHtml(html)`: prefers rendered DOM text, falls back to embedded posting JSON when DOM is empty/too short. Two carriers: `<script type="application/ld+json">` `@type:JobPosting` (schema.org — Greenhouse/LinkedIn/many boards; standardized `description`) and `<script id="__NEXT_DATA__">` (Next.js; Dayforce nests the posting under a node with `jobTitle` + `jobPostingContent` — `findNextDataJobNode` anchors on that **pair** so it won't grab the i18n string dictionary the blob also carries, which has innocuous keys like `"description":"Description"`). All extracted fields run through `stripHtmlToText` (cheerio strip tags + decode entities). `fetchVisibleText` now delegates its tail to this fn. New `MIN_POSTING_TEXT_CHARS = 30` constant replaces the magic `< 30`. Workday + pure-XHR pages still fall through to the too-short error → user pastes (the message already points at the paste tab).

- **Date:** 2026-05-28 (cross-watchlist duplicate postings in the side feed — diagnosed + fixed, working tree to be committed in this same logical step). User saw duplicate jobs in "Side postings", some already applied for, and suspected overlapping watchlists. **Diagnosed (dev.db):** two side watchlists — `security officer — Los Angeles` and `security officer — Downey, CA` (Downey ⊂ LA metro) — both keyword "security officer", so LinkedIn returns the same jobs for both. `JobPosting`'s unique key is **per-watchlist** (`@@unique([watchlistId, externalId])`), so each watchlist stores its OWN row for the same job → **94 jobs duplicated across the two, 188 of 243 side rows (~77%)**. The scheduler's existence check is per-watchlist so it never sees the twin (user's hypothesis #2 — same watcher re-importing — was NOT happening; confirmed all dup sets span exactly 2 distinct watchlists). Compounding bug: `track-as-application.ts` flipped only the clicked row to `tracked`, leaving its twin as `new` in discovery → the "already applied but still showing" symptom (7 such jobs). User chose feed-dedup + flip-siblings (keep both watchlists), then asked for a key resistant to BOTH same-URL and different-URL (LinkedIn repost) duplicates. **Shipped:**
    - **`lib/postings/dedup-key.ts`** (new) — `postingDedupKey(company, title)` = `normalizeCompanyName(company).toLowerCase()` + NUL + `normalizeRoleName(title)`. Reuses the exact Application-level normalizers, so a posting and the Application it'd become share one identity. Resistant to sourceUrl drift (LinkedIn reposts under a new id), title-punctuation drift, legal-suffix drift, and employment-modality noise — but narrow enough to keep genuine multi-role postings distinct (Studio vs Mall vs Museum Patrol). Chosen over `externalId` (= sha256(company|title|**sourceUrl**)), which folds the URL into the hash and so over-splits reposts.
    - **`app/api/postings/route.ts`** — feed-level dedup: after negative-filter, collapse `filtered` by `postingDedupKey` (Set keep-first; rows are `lastSeenAt`-desc so first = freshest), before the `limit` slice. N-way by construction (a Set collapses 2 or 200 rows identically), so adding a statewide `— California` watchlist on top is safe.
    - **`lib/postings/track-as-application.ts`** — new `flipSiblingPostings(tx, userId, {id, company, title, track})` called inside both the create-tx and the merge-link tx. Fetches the bounded `status="new"` set for the same user + **track** (JobPosting stores raw company/title, so the normalized key can't be a SQL filter — fetch + JS-filter), matches on `postingDedupKey`, and `updateMany`s every match → `tracked`. So tracking ONE posting clears every same-job row from discovery regardless of which/how many watchlists surfaced it, and regardless of externalId drift. Scoped to the same track (mirrors the per-track feed + per-track Application unique). Removed the now-used `void userId` in `mergeLinkExistingApplication`; widened its `posting` param to carry `title` + `watchlist.track`.
    - **`scripts/tests/debug/backfill-posting-dedup-flip.ts`** (new) — one-time retroactive flip: any `status="new"` posting sharing a (user, track, dedupKey) with a `tracked` posting → `tracked`. Idempotent, `--dry` preview. Ran on dev.db: flipped **2** rows the storage-key-based pass would have missed (two "Studio Patrol" reposts under different sourceUrls/externalIds — exactly the URL-drift case). (An earlier externalId-keyed SQL backfill in the same session already flipped 7 same-URL lingering twins.)
    - **`scripts/tests/hermetic/track-as-application-sibling-flip-smoke.ts`** (new, 11 assertions) — Part A (no DB): key collapses punctuation/suffix/modality drift, keeps Mall≠Studio and distinct company words distinct. Part B (DB): 3 overlapping side watchlists + 1 career, same job with different externalId/url/title/company-suffix in each → track one, assert all side siblings flip (incl. the different-externalId one), Mall Patrol stays `new` (multi-role preserved), career row stays `new` (cross-track isolation). Wired into `scripts/pre-push.sh` SUITES.

- **Date:** 2026-05-28 (auto-generated API reference — kills the stale-`apis.md` problem). User asked for a utility that generates API docs from the route code so `docs/apis.md` doesn't rot as routes grow. Built a custom generator (option #2 of: off-the-shelf `next-swagger-doc` / custom generator / framework adoption) because the repo's Zod-v4 dep gives `z.toJSONSchema` for free and it fits the in-progress HTML-docs migration. **Shipped:**
    - **`scripts/gen-api-docs.ts`** (new, `npm run gen:api-docs`) — statically AST-parses (TypeScript compiler API; routes are **never executed**) all 61 `app/api/**/route.ts` for the facts that go stale: HTTP methods (both `export async function GET` and `export const GET =` styles), auth guard (any identifier imported from `lib/auth-guards` that's invoked — catches `requireSession`/`requireLocalOrSession`/`requireSessionOrService` — plus inline `getServerSession`), and `withCache` TTL + upstreamHost (handles both the options-object and bare-number arg styles, and resolves top-level `const` TTL/host references like `SATELLITE_TTL_SECONDS`/`UPSTREAM_HOST`; dynamic host fns → host omitted, not guessed). Request bodies render from the route's Zod schema via `z.toJSONSchema(schema, { io: 'input' })` (input mode = pre-transform client shape; survives `.transform()`/`.coerce` that plain `toJSONSchema` chokes on). Imports only the pure `lib/schemas/*` modules. Emits `docs/apis.html` from the shared template/stylesheet. `--check` mode = exit 1 if the committed HTML drifts (ignores the informational date line).
    - **`lib/api-docs/meta.ts`** (new) — `ApiMeta` type for the one un-inferable bit: `export const apiMeta: ApiMeta = { purpose, external?, notes?, methods? }`. Plain object literal (read statically, not run). **It lives in a sibling `meta.ts` next to each route (e.g. `app/api/ai/meta.ts`), NOT in `route.ts`.** Critical gotcha discovered mid-build: Next.js validates a route module's named exports (generated `.next/types/**/route.ts` uses an `OmitWithTag<…, "">` check), so an `apiMeta` export in `route.ts` is a build/`tsc` error (no `typescript.ignoreBuildErrors` in next.config, and `.next/types/**` is in tsconfig include → 61 errors). The sidecar isn't a route file so it escapes validation, is never bundled, and is still colocated (co-edited in the same PR). The 61 `route.ts` files are therefore **pristine vs HEAD** — all metadata is in the new `meta.ts` files.
    - **`docs/apis.html`** (new, generated) + **API CSS** appended to `docs/assets/style.css` (`.api-route`, `.api-method.{get,post,patch,put,delete}` verb badges, `.api-chip.{auth,cache,ext}`, schema blocks).
    - **All 61 routes documented.** Seeded 8 by hand (ai, calendar/event, space/moon, gmail/webhook, tasks, finance, applications, space/satellites — chosen to exercise every extraction path), then backfilled the remaining 53 via 5 parallel subagents (porting prose from old `apis.md` where it existed, deriving from code otherwise). A one-time AST migration script relocated every `apiMeta` from `route.ts` → sibling `meta.ts` after the Next-export gotcha surfaced (script since deleted).

All three CDNs cache after first load; offline → code degrades to flat green, diagrams render static.

CONVENTION: every section carries ≥1 *named* `<h3>` (its `X.1`) so any content is referenceable as `X.Y` even when there's only one — authors write just the name, no manual prefix; only `<h3>` is numbered (`<h4>` isn't). Applied to `architecture.html` (stripped the 34 manual `N.M ` prefixes; added a named `X.1` to the 11 subsection-less sections — e.g. 16.1 Summary, 1.1 Operating Context). - **Date:** 2026-05-27 (multi-role-per-company dedup — dev.db + prod.db BOTH migrated, working tree to be committed in this same logical step). User reported a 500 when clicking "Track as app" on the Allied Universal "Security Officer Part Time Museum Rover" LinkedIn posting in dev. Root cause: schema's `@@unique([userId, normalizedCompany, track])` made a second Allied Universal app on the side kanban (the user already had a different Allied role linked to a different posting) impossible — the P2002 caught in `lib/postings/track-as-application.ts:104` only handled the postingId-race recovery, so the company-track collision rethrew → 500. User reframed the bug: it should be legal to have multiple applications at the same company for different positions, but we need more data than just the company name to distinguish them. Operator picked **Rule B** (keep parens content as additional tokens) for role normalization. **Shipped:**
    - **`lib/applications/normalize-role.ts`** (new). Rule B normalizer: lowercase + NFKC, punctuation (including parens) → token separators, drop noise tokens (part/time/full/pt/ft/remote/hybrid/onsite/contract/contractor/temp/intern/internship/permanent + light articles), preserve substantive modifiers (senior/staff/lead/principal/junior naturally — not in the drop list). Idempotent. Worked example: `"Security Officer Part Time Museum Rover"` → `"security officer museum rover"`; `"Part-Time Security Officer (Museum)"` → `"security officer museum"` — these are now legitimately distinct rows.
    - **`prisma/schema.prisma`** — added nullable `normalizedRole` + `sourceJobId` columns; swapped unique from `(userId, normalizedCompany, track)` → `(userId, normalizedCompany, normalizedRole, track)`; new `@@index([userId, sourceJobId])`.
    - **Two migrations** applied to BOTH dev.db AND prod.db (each tier's PM2 web + scheduler briefly stopped):
        - `20260527230000_add_application_role_columns` — nullable columns only.
        - `20260527231500_swap_application_unique_for_role` — drops old unique, creates new + index. Phase-2 gated on backfill collision audit ✓.
    - **`scripts/backfill-normalized-role.ts`** (new) — populates `normalizedRole` for all rows + `sourceJobId` from `postingId → posting.externalId`. Includes a collision audit on the future unique quadruple. Ran clean on both DBs: dev.db **46 rows updated, 29 sourceJobIds populated, 0 collisions**; prod.db **45 rows updated, 27 sourceJobIds populated, 0 collisions**. Sanity-check before running migrate on prod confirmed zero pre-existing duplicates on the OLD `(userId, normalizedCompany, track)` triple, which mathematically guarantees the new quadruple unique can't collide either (NULL-distinct during phase 2, and post-backfill the column adds CAN'T create a new violation on a previously-deduped triple).
    - **`lib/repositories/applications.ts`** — `ApplicationCreate` gains optional `normalizedRole` + `sourceJobId` (auto-derived in `createApplication`). `updateApplication` keeps `normalizedRole` in sync when `role` changes (with a guard against poisoning the key with empty normalize output). Two new helpers: `findApplicationByCompanyAndRole(userId, company, role, track?)` and `findApplicationBySourceJobId(userId, sourceJobId)`. `bulkMoveApplicationsTrack` conflict detection now keys on the (company, role) pair — same-company different-role moves succeed (which they couldn't pre-fix).
    - **`lib/applications/ingest.ts`** — dedup priority: (1) `findApplicationByCompanyAndRole` cross-track + senderDomain tie-breaker; (2) legacy company-only fallback for NULL-normalizedRole rows (transitional safety net, prints warn pointing at backfill script); (3) `findApplicationBySenderDomain` CSULB-drift fallback; (4) create. P2002 race-recovery now uses the role-aware lookup with company-only fallback.
    - **`lib/postings/track-as-application.ts`** — new dedup chain: (1) same posting twice (idempotent); (2) `findApplicationBySourceJobId` for same job via different posting row; (3) `findApplicationByCompanyAndRole` scoped to watchlist track; (4) create. Cases 2+3 use **merge-link semantics**: don't overwrite existing `postingId`, log NOTE event ("Tracked from …" if linking, "Also saw …" if not), flip new posting to "tracked", return `merged=true` `created=false`. Brand-new create writes both normalized keys + sourceJobId inline. P2002 catch handles both racing cases (postingId vs. company+role+track).
    - **`TrackResult` type + `app/api/postings/[id]/track-as-application/route.ts` + `lib/api-client.ts`** — added `merged: boolean` to the success response. Client-side schema accepts it as optional (backwards-compat).
    - **`scripts/tests/hermetic/normalize-role-smoke.ts`** (new, 23 assertions, pure function): basic shape, the museum-rover/mall-patrol distinction, Rule B parens-as-tokens, modality stripping, modifier preservation, punctuation handling, idempotency, all-noise → empty.
    - **`scripts/tests/hermetic/track-as-application-multi-role-smoke.ts`** (new, 27 assertions): case 1 same company different role → two apps coexist (the bug regression test); case 2 same company same role different posting → merge-link, original postingId preserved, "Also saw" NOTE event recorded; case 3 manual-created app with NULL postingId → merge-link with linkage (postingId set, sourceJobId stamped); case 4 same posting twice → idempotent created=false merged=false.

- **Date:** 2026-05-27 (Gmail-ingest cross-track dedup + explicit-track invariant — UNCOMMITTED). User reported a Mattel application email did not move their existing `Mattel, Inc.` side-track kanban row to APPLIED. Root cause: `lib/applications/ingest.ts:131` hardcoded `const ingestTrack = "career"` and passed it as the lookup scope to both `findApplicationByCompany` and `findApplicationBySenderDomain`. A user's manual side-track row was structurally invisible to dedup — ingest spawned a new career-track Mattel row instead of updating the side row. Compounding leak: `lib/postings/track-as-application.ts:57` bypassed the `createApplication` helper (writes through `tx.application.create({})` to stay inside the watchlist→application transaction), so every "Track this posting" promotion landed with `normalizedCompany=null`. 30 such rows in dev.db. **Shipped:**

Both lookup helpers gained an optional third arg: `findApplicationByCompany(userId, company, track?)` and `findApplicationBySenderDomain(userId, domain, track?)` — when omitted, the track predicate drops and the lookup spans both kanbans.     - **`lib/applications/ingest.ts`** — rewrote the dedup block (lines 119–144). Lookups now cross-track. Added a sender-domain tie-breaker: when a company match exists AND the email's sender domain differs from the matched row's stored domain, look across tracks for a same-company sibling whose `senderDomain` matches; switch to it if found (guarded by `normalizeCompanyName(byDomain.company) === normalizeCompanyName(existingApp.company)` so CSULB-drift unrelated employers don't cause a wrong switch). Brand-new-row branch now sets `track: "career"` as an **explicit literal** at the call site — no `?? "career"`, no schema default. Race-recovery `findApplicationByCompany` at the P2002 catch is also cross-track now (so a race against track-as-application resolves correctly when the winner landed on `side`).

- **Date:** 2026-05-27 (lockstep employment-type classifier). User flagged Lunary showing 2 `employment-type-classifier` calls a few minutes apart every 30–50 min and asked whether the cadence could be batched to save tokens/spend. Diagnosed: `scheduler/jobs/job-watcher.ts` fires its own classifier batch per watchlist per tick whenever new postings land + the heuristic returns null — 39 active watchlists in dev.db (37 @ 240min, 2 @ 60min) with offset `lastRunAt` clocks means the 10-min scheduler tick scatters small classifier batches across the day. **Refactor (user's design):** keep the inline batch ONLY on a watchlist's first crawl (`watchlist.lastSuccessAt === null`) so newly-added watchlists feel responsive; everything else writes new postings with `employmentType=null` and waits for a new lockstep sweep. **Shipped:**
    - **`scheduler/jobs/job-watcher.ts`** — wrapped the `classifyEmploymentTypes` call's input builder in `isFirstRun ? […] : []` so non-first-run new postings skip the inline LLM call. The cross-watchlist reuse block above it (lines ~219–253) still runs and still hydrates raw.employmentType from a sibling's stored value when present — that path is FREE (no LLM call) so it stays unconditional.
    - **`scheduler/jobs/classify-pending-employment-types.ts`** (new) — `runClassifyPendingEmploymentTypes(chatFn?)` selects every `JobPosting WHERE employmentType IS NULL AND status NOT IN ('closed','hidden')` ordered by `firstSeenAt ASC`, dedupes by externalId (caps at `SWEEP_CAP=1000` distinct), calls `classifyEmploymentTypes`, then `updateMany` per externalId with `employmentType: null` race guard. `chatFn` parameter forwards to the shared `ChatJSONFn` injection seam — same hermetic pattern as `lib/ai/classify-employment-type.ts`.
    - **`scheduler/index.ts`** — new IntervalJob entry at `4 * 60 * 60 * 1000` (4h) cadence. The 10s-per-job startup stagger already in place means it kicks at boot+30s.

User flagged that only `employment-type-classifier` currently uses `MODEL_LITE_CHEAP` (`gemini-2.5-flash-lite`) and asked whether other picker/enum-shaped callsites could safely move down a tier.   - **Override hook** in `lib/ai/gemini.ts:chatJSON` — when `MC_EVAL_DOWNGRADE_CALLSITES` (comma-separated callsite `name:` values) and `MC_EVAL_DOWNGRADE_MODEL` (gemini model id) are both set, the named callsites' model swaps to the downgrade model for that call. Other callsites in the same run stay on their hardcoded models. Prod never sets these env vars; the hunk is a true no-op there.
  - **Probe driver** `scripts/tests/probes/eval-downgrade-probe.ts` runs `promptfoo eval` twice (baseline + downgrade), writes `eval/output/probe-{baseline,downgrade}.json`, and prints a per-callsite × per-assertion pass-rate diff. - **Findings (two probe runs):** `bullet-tags-from-posting` passed 4/4 → 4/4 on the original fixtures, then **regressed 9/9 → 8/9** after the expanded fixtures caught the cheap model tagging "Built the public-facing marketing site as a React SPA with Next.js" as `React Native`. Classic close-but-not-match false positive — MODEL_LITE correctly returned `{"proposals":[]}` on the same fixture. **`bullet-tags-from-profile`** stays on MODEL_LITE — the bartending cross-domain fixture is rubric-noise between runs (5/6 baseline, then 6/6 the next pass) but the regression is real enough not to flip. **`discovery-suggest`** survives 3/3 → 3/3 with the expanded fixtures, but user pushed back (correctly) that 3 fixtures is too thin given that the assertions are all hard-rule checks (shape + excludes-respected + internal-uniqueness) and don't catch the soft quality drop most likely on the cheaper model — suggestion plausibility, topic adherence, diversity. **Decision: don't flip anything yet.** Net cost of this whole exploration: ~$0.10 in Gemini spend across the probe runs.
- **Open follow-ups for this exploration:**
  - **Before flipping `discovery-suggest` to `MODEL_LITE_CHEAP`** — expand `eval/suites/discovery-suggest.yaml` to 5–7 fixtures (cover ambiguous-topic like "shell", broad-topic like "fintech", niche like "fusion energy", no-excludes-diversity test). Add an `llm-rubric` assertion per fixture grading suggestion *plausibility* ("Are at least 3 of these recognizable real companies that fit the topic?") since the current hard-rule assertions survive a quality drop. Then re-run the probe. Cost: ~5–20 extra outbound HTTP probes per new fixture; ~$0.05 extra Gemini.

- **Date:** 2026-05-26 (mobile shell — pagination chevrons for fine-pointer devices). User flagged that shrinking the desktop browser window kicks the app into mobile mode (great), but the mobile shell relies on horizontal swipe for dash navigation and a mouse can't swipe cleanly. Fix: new `useFinePointer()` hook in `hooks/useMobileLayout.ts` watches `matchMedia('(pointer: fine)')` (SSR-safe: returns false on server / first client render, settles to real matches once mounted). `components/dashboard/MobileShell.tsx` now renders small prev/next chevron buttons (left/right vertical-center, smaller than DesktopShell's chevrons) when `hasFinePointer && len > 1 && !isLaunchpadOpen` — real touch devices (`pointer: coarse`) keep the swipe-only look; small desktop windows get pagination buttons alongside swipe. The standard `(pointer: fine)` test correctly classifies hybrid devices (Magic-Keyboard iPad, Surface laptop) as fine when the user's primary input is a pointing device, which is the right behavior. `tsc --noEmit` clean. Lint flag on `setFine(mql.matches)` synchronously in effect is a pre-existing pattern (same warning fires on `useMobileLayout`'s `setIsMobile`); pre-push doesn't actually run lint (the echo line "hermetic suite + lint" is stale — script only runs hermetic SUITES).

- **Date:** 2026-05-26 (1-page resume toggle — UNCOMMITTED, feature is live in PM2 dev). Shipped: new `lib/resumes/one-page.ts` with `pruneOneStep` (drops the lowest-aggregate-score removable entity first; falls back to dropping the lowest-scoring non-locked bullet from any entity with ≥ 2 bullets) and `renderResumePDFOnePage` (iterative loop: compose props → `renderResumePDF` → `pdf-parse` `getInfo().total` for page count → prune → repeat, cap at `MAX_PRUNE_ITERATIONS=8`). `getUnremovableEntityIds` reads `selection.{workRoles,projects,education}[0]` — those are "latest" after the selector's sort (workRoles by startDate desc, projects by position asc, education by startDate desc). Entities containing a locked bullet are implicitly unremovable via `aggregateEntityScore` returning Infinity. New hermetic `resume-one-page-prune-smoke.ts` covers 17 assertions on the pure pruner: unremovable set membership, lowest-aggregate-score wins, locked-bullet protection, bullet-prune fallback, null-when-nothing-left, global-lowest cross-section comparison. Smoke passes 17/17 standalone; wired into `scripts/pre-push.sh`. - **Date:** 2026-05-26 (resume selector spine-guard). User ran a Rocket Lab software-internship resume in dev and saw their current Security Officer @ AEG role surface despite scoring 0 against the posting keywords. Root cause: `lib/resumes/select.ts:selectBullets` passed `keepAlways: (_e, i) => i === 0` for work roles — the most-recent role was kept unconditionally as the work-role spine, even when completely off-topic. Fix: new `pickWorkRoleSpineIndex(workRoles, keywords)` helper picks the spine slot — defaults to index 0 when that role's top bullet scores ≥ `MIN_KEEP_SCORE` (= `TAG_WEIGHT` = 2), otherwise falls back to whichever role scores highest. Final fallback when every role is below threshold: returns 0 anyway (preserves no-empty-work-role-section invariant). Two new hermetic regression checks (8c + 8d) on `resume-select-smoke.ts`: (8c) off-topic recent + relevant older → older becomes spine and recent dropped; (8d) all roles off-topic → most-recent still kept as fallback. `resume-select-smoke` now 14/14 green. **Note (pre-existing failure outside this fix, not caused by this change):** `prompt-render-smoke` reports `[FAIL] resume-tagline: every declared {{var}} has a sample — missing: entityIdsBlock`. Comes from the user's pre-existing uncommitted edits to `docs/llm-prompts/resume-tagline.md` post-`2034261` — confirmed via `git stash` round-trip showing 166/166 green without the uncommitted tree. **Still NOT addressed in this run** (user wants to make these calls themselves before code changes): (a) mysubs.live's broad autoTags ("Software Engineering", "Web Applications") — the user can × them in the Profile UI to push them into the bullet's `removedTags` blocklist, or we tighten `bullet-tags-from-posting` prompt against very-generic posting keywords on bog-standard CRUD bullets.
